Protection: prevent fraudulent attacks from bots and humans&quot;],&quot;description&quot;:[0,&quot;Blocking bots isnât enough anymore. Cloudflareâs new fraud prevention capabilities â now available in Early Access â help stop account abuse before it starts.&quot;],&quot;imgPreview&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1Aj9h1PNF8IZyAQNhjzZuA/ed5eb29187ef89e8019aea5b2dcfe747/OG_Share_2024-2025-2026__22_.png&quot;]}],&quot;publicly_index&quot;:[0,true]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;46xdz0GQfFtpCKRKNbfj3b&quot;],&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;Slashing agent token costs by 98% with RFC 9457-compliant error responses&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;rfc-9457-agent-error-pages&quot;],&quot;excerpt&quot;:[0,&quot;Cloudflare now returns RFC 9457-compliant structured Markdown and JSON error payloads to AI agents, replacing heavyweight HTML pages with machine-readable instructions. This reduces token usage by over 98%, turning brittle parsing into efficient control flow.&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;AI agents are no longer experiments. They are production infrastructure, making billions of HTTP requests per day, navigating the web, calling APIs, and orchestrating complex workflows.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;But when these agents hit an error, they still receive the same HTML error pages we built for browsers: hundreds of lines of markup, CSS, and copy designed for human eyes. Those pages give agents clues, not instructions, and waste time and tokens. That gap is the opportunity to give agents instructions, not obstacles.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Starting today, Cloudflare returns &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9457\&quot;&gt;RFC 9457&lt;/a&gt;-compliant structured Markdown and JSON error payloads to AI agents, replacing heavyweight HTML pages with machine-readable instructions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That means when an agent sends &lt;code&gt;Accept: text/markdown&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/json&lt;/code&gt;, or &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/problem+json&lt;/code&gt; and encounters a Cloudflare error, we return one semantic contract in a structured format instead of HTML. And it comes complete with actionable guidance. (This builds on our recent &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/markdown-for-agents/\&quot;&gt;Markdown for Agents&lt;/a&gt; release.)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;So instead of being told only &amp;quot;You were blocked,&amp;quot; the agent will read: &amp;quot;You were rate-limited â wait 30 seconds and retry with exponential backoff.&amp;quot; Instead of just &amp;quot;Access denied,&amp;quot; the agent will be instructed: &amp;quot;This block is intentional: do not retry, contact the site owner.&amp;quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;These responses are not just clearer â they are dramatically more efficient. Structured error responses cut payload size and token usage by more than 98% versus HTML, measured against a live 1015 (&amp;#39;rate-limit&amp;#39;) error response. For agents that hit multiple errors in a workflow, the savings compound quickly.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is live across the Cloudflare network, automatically. Site owners do not need to configure anything. Browsers keep getting the same HTML experience as before.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;These are not just error pages. They are instructions for the agentic web.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;what-agents-see-today\&quot;&gt;What agents see today&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-agents-see-today\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;When an agent receives a Cloudflare-generated error, it usually means Cloudflare is enforcing customer policy or returning a platform response on the customer&amp;#39;s behalf â not that Cloudflare is down. These responses are triggered when a request cannot be served as-is, such as invalid host or DNS routing, customer-defined access controls (WAF, geo, ASN, or bot rules), or edge-enforced limits like rate limiting. In short, Cloudflare is acting as the customer&amp;#39;s routing and security layer, and the response explains why the request was blocked or could not proceed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, those responses are rendered as HTML designed for humans:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-HTML\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-HTML\&quot;&gt;&amp;lt;!DOCTYPE html&amp;gt;\n&amp;lt;html&amp;gt;\n&amp;lt;head&amp;gt;\n&amp;lt;title&amp;gt;Access denied | example.com used Cloudflare to restrict access&amp;lt;/title&amp;gt;\n&amp;lt;style&amp;gt;/* 200 lines of CSS */&amp;lt;/style&amp;gt;\n&amp;lt;/head&amp;gt;\n&amp;lt;body&amp;gt;\n  &amp;lt;div class=&amp;quot;cf-wrapper&amp;quot;&amp;gt;\n    &amp;lt;h1 data-translate=&amp;quot;block_headline&amp;quot;&amp;gt;Sorry, you have been blocked&amp;lt;/h1&amp;gt;\n    &amp;lt;!-- ... hundreds more lines ... --&amp;gt;\n  &amp;lt;/div&amp;gt;\n&amp;lt;/body&amp;gt;\n&amp;lt;/html&amp;gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;To an agent, this is garbage. It cannot determine what error occurred, why it was blocked, or whether retrying will help. Even if it parses the HTML, the content describes the error but doesn&amp;#39;t tell the agent â or the human, for that matter â what to do next.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#39;re an agent developer and you wanted to handle Cloudflare errors gracefully, your options were limited. For Cloudflare-generated errors, structured responses existed only in configuration-dependent paths, not as a consistent default for agents.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Custom Error Rules can customize many Cloudflare errors, including some 1xxx cases. But they depend on per-site configuration, so they cannot serve as a universal agent contract across the web. Cloudflare sits in front of the request path. That means we can define a default machine response: retry or stop, wait and back off, escalate or reroute. Error pages stop being decoration and become execution instructions.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;what-we-did\&quot;&gt;What we did&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-we-did\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Cloudflare now returns RFC 9457-compliant structured responses for all 1xxx-class error paths â Cloudflare&amp;#39;s platform error codes for edge-side failures like DNS resolution issues, access denials, and rate limits. Both formats are live: &lt;code&gt;Accept: text/markdown&lt;/code&gt; returns Markdown, &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/json&lt;/code&gt; returns JSON, and &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/problem+json&lt;/code&gt; returns JSON with the &lt;code&gt;application/problem+json&lt;/code&gt; content type.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This covers all 1xxx-class errors today. The same contract will extend to Cloudflare-generated 4xx and 5xx errors next.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Markdown responses have two parts:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;YAML frontmatter for machine-readable fields&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;prose sections for explicit guidance (&lt;code&gt;What happened&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;What you should do&lt;/code&gt;)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;JSON responses carry the same fields as a flat object.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The YAML frontmatter is the critical layer for automation. It lets an agent extract stable keys without scraping HTML or guessing intent from copy. Fields like &lt;code&gt;error_code&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;error_name&lt;/code&gt;, and &lt;code&gt;error_category&lt;/code&gt; let the agent classify the failure. &lt;code&gt;retryable&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;retry_after&lt;/code&gt; drive backoff logic. &lt;code&gt;owner_action_required&lt;/code&gt; tells the agent whether to keep trying or escalate. &lt;code&gt;ray_id&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;timestamp&lt;/code&gt;, and &lt;code&gt;zone&lt;/code&gt; make logs and support handoffs deterministic.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The schema is stable by design, so agents can implement durable control flow without chasing presentation changes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That stability is not a Cloudflare invention. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9457\&quot;&gt;RFC 9457 â Problem Details for HTTP APIs&lt;/a&gt; defines a standard JSON shape for reporting errors over HTTP, so clients can parse error responses without knowing the specific API in advance. Our JSON responses follow this shape, which means any HTTP client that understands Problem Details can parse the base members without Cloudflare-specific code:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;RFC 9457 member&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;What it contains&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;type&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;A URI pointing to Cloudflare&amp;#39;s documentation for the specific error code&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;status&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The HTTP status code (matching the actual response status)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;title&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;A short, human-readable summary of the problem&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;detail&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;A human-readable explanation specific to this occurrence&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;instance&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The Ray ID identifying this specific error occurrence&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;The operational fields â &lt;code&gt;error_code&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;error_category&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;retryable&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;retry_after&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;owner_action_required&lt;/code&gt;, and more â are RFC 9457 extension members. Clients that don&amp;#39;t recognize them simply ignore them.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is network-wide and additive. Site owners do not need to configure anything. Browsers keep receiving HTML unless clients explicitly ask for Markdown or JSON.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;what-the-response-looks-like\&quot;&gt;What the response looks like&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-the-response-looks-like\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Here is what a rate-limit error (&lt;code&gt;1015&lt;/code&gt;) looks like in JSON:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-JSON\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-JSON\&quot;&gt;{\n  &amp;quot;type&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/support/troubleshooting/http-status-codes/cloudflare-1xxx-errors/error-1015/&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;title&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;Error 1015: You are being rate limited&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;status&amp;quot;: 429,\n  &amp;quot;detail&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;You are being rate-limited by the website owner&amp;#039;s configuration.&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;instance&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;9d99a4434fz2d168&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;error_code&amp;quot;: 1015,\n  &amp;quot;error_name&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;rate_limited&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;error_category&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;rate_limit&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;ray_id&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;9d99a4434fz2d168&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;timestamp&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;2026-03-09T11:11:55Z&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;zone&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;&amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;cloudflare_error&amp;quot;: true,\n  &amp;quot;retryable&amp;quot;: true,\n  &amp;quot;retry_after&amp;quot;: 30,\n  &amp;quot;owner_action_required&amp;quot;: false,\n  &amp;quot;what_you_should_do&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;**Wait and retry.** This block is transient. Wait at least 30 seconds, then retry with exponential backoff.\\n\\nRecommended approach:\\n1. Wait 30 seconds before your next request\\n2. If rate-limited again, double the wait time (60s, 120s, etc.)\\n3. If rate-limiting persists after 5 retries, stop and reassess your request pattern&amp;quot;,\n  &amp;quot;footer&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;This error was generated by Cloudflare on behalf of the website owner.&amp;quot;\n}&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;The same error in Markdown, optimized for model-first workflows:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Markdown\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Markdown\&quot;&gt;---\nerror_code: 1015\nerror_name: rate_limited\nerror_category: rate_limit\nstatus: 429\nray_id: 9d99a39dc992d168\ntimestamp: 2026-03-09T11:11:28Z\nzone: &amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;\ncloudflare_error: true\nretryable: true\nretry_after: 30\nowner_action_required: false\n---\n\n# Error 1015: You are being rate limited\n\n## What Happened\n\nYou are being rate-limited by the website owner&amp;#039;s configuration.\n\n## What You Should Do\n\n**Wait and retry.** This block is transient. Wait at least 30 seconds, then retry with exponential backoff.\n\nRecommended approach:\n1. Wait 30 seconds before your next request\n2. If rate-limited again, double the wait time (60s, 120s, etc.)\n3. If rate-limiting persists after 5 retries, stop and reassess your request pattern\n\n---\nThis error was generated by Cloudflare on behalf of the website owner.\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;Both formats give an agent everything it needs to decide and act: classify the error, choose retry behavior, and determine whether escalation is required. This is what a default machine contract looks like â not per-site configuration, but network-wide behavior. The contrast is explicit across error families: a transient error like &lt;code&gt;1015&lt;/code&gt; says wait and retry, while intentional blocks like &lt;code&gt;1020&lt;/code&gt; or geographic restrictions like &lt;code&gt;1009&lt;/code&gt; tell the agent not to retry and to escalate instead.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;one-contract-two-formats\&quot;&gt;One contract, two formats&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#one-contract-two-formats\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The core value is not format choice. It is semantic stability.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Agents need deterministic answers to operational questions: retry or not, how long to wait, and whether to escalate. Cloudflare exposes one policy contract across two wire formats. Whether a client consumes Markdown or JSON, the operational meaning is identical: same error identity, same retry/backoff signals, same escalation guidance.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Clients that send &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/problem+json&lt;/code&gt; get &lt;code&gt;application/problem+json; charset=utf-8&lt;/code&gt; back â useful for HTTP client libraries that dispatch on media type. Clients that send &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/json&lt;/code&gt; get &lt;code&gt;application/json; charset=utf-8&lt;/code&gt; â same body, safe default for existing consumers.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;size-reduction-and-token-efficiency\&quot;&gt;Size reduction and token efficiency&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#size-reduction-and-token-efficiency\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;That contract is also dramatically smaller than what it replaces. Cloudflare HTML error pages are browser-oriented and heavy, while structured responses are compact by design.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Measured comparison for &lt;code&gt;1015&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Payload&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Bytes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Tokens (cl100k_base)&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Size vs HTML&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Token vs HTML&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;HTML response&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;46,645&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;14,252&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;â&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;â&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Markdown response&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;798&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;221&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;58.5x less&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;64.5x less&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;JSON response&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;970&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;256&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;48.1x less&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;55.7x less&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;Both structured formats deliver a ~98% reduction in size and tokens versus HTML. For agents, size translates directly into token cost â when an agent hits multiple errors in one run, these savings compound into lower model spend and faster recovery loops.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;ten-categories-clear-actions\&quot;&gt;Ten categories, clear actions&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#ten-categories-clear-actions\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Every &lt;code&gt;1xxx&lt;/code&gt; error is mapped to an &lt;code&gt;error_category&lt;/code&gt;. That turns error handling into routing logic instead of brittle per-page parsing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Category&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;What it means&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;What the agent should do&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;access_denied&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Intentional block: IP, ASN, geo, firewall rule&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Do not retry. Contact site owner if unexpected.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;rate_limit&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Request rate exceeded&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Back off. Retry after retry_after seconds.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;dns&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;DNS resolution failure at the origin&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Do not retry. Report to site owner.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;config&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Configuration error: CNAME, tunnel, host routing&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Do not retry (usually). Report to site owner.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;tls&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;TLS version or cipher mismatch&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Fix TLS client settings. Do not retry as-is.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;legal&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;DMCA or regulatory block&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Do not retry. This is a legal restriction.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;worker&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflare Workers runtime error&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Do not retry. Site owner must fix the script.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;rewrite&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Invalid URL rewrite output&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Do not retry. Site owner must fix the rule.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;snippet&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflare Snippets error&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Do not retry. Site owner must fix Snippets config.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;unsupported&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Unsupported method or deprecated feature&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Change the request. Do not retry as-is.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;Two fields make this operationally useful for agents:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;retryable&lt;/code&gt; answers whether a retry can succeed&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;owner_action_required&lt;/code&gt; answers whether the problem must be escalated&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can replace brittle &amp;quot;if status == 429 then maybe retry&amp;quot; heuristics with explicit control flow. Parse the frontmatter once, then branch on stable fields. A simple pattern is:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;if &lt;code&gt;retryable&lt;/code&gt; is &lt;code&gt;true&lt;/code&gt;, wait &lt;code&gt;retry_after&lt;/code&gt; and retry&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;if &lt;code&gt;owner_action_required&lt;/code&gt; is &lt;code&gt;true&lt;/code&gt;, stop and escalate&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;otherwise, fail fast without hammering the site&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Here is a minimal Python example using that pattern:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Python\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Python\&quot;&gt;import time\nimport yaml\n\n\ndef parse_frontmatter(markdown_text: str) -&amp;gt; dict:\n    # Expects: ---\\n&amp;lt;yaml&amp;gt;\\n---\\n&amp;lt;body&amp;gt;\n    if not markdown_text.startswith(&amp;quot;---\\n&amp;quot;):\n        return {}\n    _, yaml_block, _ = markdown_text.split(&amp;quot;---\\n&amp;quot;, 2)\n    return yaml.safe_load(yaml_block) or {}\n\n\ndef handle_cloudflare_error(markdown_text: str) -&amp;gt; str:\n    meta = parse_frontmatter(markdown_text)\n\n    if not meta.get(&amp;quot;cloudflare_error&amp;quot;):\n        return &amp;quot;not_cloudflare_error&amp;quot;\n\n    if meta.get(&amp;quot;retryable&amp;quot;):\n        wait_seconds = int(meta.get(&amp;quot;retry_after&amp;quot;, 30))\n        time.sleep(wait_seconds)\n        return f&amp;quot;retry_after_{wait_seconds}s&amp;quot;\n\n    if meta.get(&amp;quot;owner_action_required&amp;quot;):\n        return f&amp;quot;escalate_owner_error_{meta.get(&amp;#039;error_code&amp;#039;)}&amp;quot;\n\n    return &amp;quot;do_not_retry&amp;quot;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;This is the key shift: agents are no longer inferring intent from HTML copy. They are executing explicit policy from structured fields.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-to-use-it\&quot;&gt;How to use it&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-to-use-it\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Send &lt;code&gt;Accept: text/markdown&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/json&lt;/code&gt;, or &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/problem+json&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For quick testing, you can hit any Cloudflare-proxied domain directly at &lt;code&gt;/cdn-cgi/error/1015&lt;/code&gt; (or replace &lt;code&gt;1015&lt;/code&gt; with another &lt;code&gt;1xxx&lt;/code&gt; code).&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;curl -s --compressed -H &amp;quot;Accept: text/markdown&amp;quot; -A &amp;quot;TestAgent/1.0&amp;quot; -H &amp;quot;Accept-Encoding: gzip, deflate&amp;quot; &amp;quot;&amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;/cdn-cgi/error/1015&amp;quot;\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;Example with another error code:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;curl -s --compressed -H &amp;quot;Accept: text/markdown&amp;quot; -A &amp;quot;TestAgent/1.0&amp;quot; -H &amp;quot;Accept-Encoding: gzip, deflate&amp;quot; &amp;quot;&amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;/cdn-cgi/error/1020&amp;quot;\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;JSON example:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-JSON\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-JSON\&quot;&gt;curl -s --compressed -H &amp;quot;Accept: application/json&amp;quot; -A &amp;quot;TestAgent/1.0&amp;quot; -H &amp;quot;Accept-Encoding: gzip, deflate&amp;quot; &amp;quot;&amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;/cdn-cgi/error/1015&amp;quot; | jq .\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;RFC 9457 Problem Details example:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;curl -s --compressed -H &amp;quot;Accept: application/problem+json&amp;quot; -A &amp;quot;TestAgent/1.0&amp;quot; -H &amp;quot;Accept-Encoding: gzip, deflate&amp;quot; &amp;quot;&amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;/cdn-cgi/error/1015&amp;quot; | jq .\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;The behavior is deterministic â the first explicit structured type wins:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Accept header&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Response&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;application/json&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;JSON&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;application/json; charset=utf-8&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;JSON&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;application/problem+json&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;JSON (application/problem+json content type)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;application/json, text/markdown;q=0.9&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;JSON&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;application/json, text/markdown&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;JSON (equal q, first-listed wins)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;text/markdown&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Markdown&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;text/markdown, application/json&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Markdown (equal q, first-listed wins)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;text/markdown, */*&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Markdown&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;text/*&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Markdown&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code&gt;*/*&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;HTML (default)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;Wildcard-only requests (&lt;code&gt;*/*&lt;/code&gt;) do not signal a structured preference; clients must explicitly request Markdown or JSON.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;If the request succeeds, you get normal origin content. The header only affects Cloudflare-generated error responses.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;real-world-use-cases\&quot;&gt;Real-world use cases&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#real-world-use-cases\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;There are a number of situations where structured error responses help immediately:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Agent blocked by WAF rule (&lt;code&gt;1020&lt;/code&gt;). The agent parses &lt;code&gt;error_code&lt;/code&gt;, records &lt;code&gt;ray_id&lt;/code&gt;, and stops retrying. It can escalate with useful context instead of looping.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;MCP (Model Context Protocol) tool hitting geo restriction (&lt;code&gt;1009&lt;/code&gt;). The tool gets a clear, machine-readable reason, returns it to the orchestrator, and the workflow can choose an alternate path or notify the user.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Rate-limited crawler (&lt;code&gt;1015&lt;/code&gt;). The agent reads &lt;code&gt;retryable&lt;/code&gt;: true and &lt;code&gt;retry_after&lt;/code&gt;, applies backoff, and retries predictably instead of hammering the endpoint.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Developer debugging with &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt;. The developer can reproduce exactly what the agent sees, including frontmatter and guidance, without reverse-engineering HTML.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;HTTP client libraries that understand RFC 9457. Any client that dispatches on &lt;code&gt;application/problem+json&lt;/code&gt; or parses Problem Details objects can handle Cloudflare errors without Cloudflare-specific code.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt;In each case, the outcome is the same: less guessing, fewer wasted retries, lower model cost, and faster recovery.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;try-it-now\&quot;&gt;Try it now&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#try-it-now\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Send a structured &lt;code&gt;Accept&lt;/code&gt; header and test against any Cloudflare-proxied domain:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;curl -s --compressed -H &amp;quot;Accept: text/markdown&amp;quot; -A &amp;quot;TestAgent/1.0&amp;quot; -H &amp;quot;Accept-Encoding: gzip, deflate&amp;quot; &amp;quot;&amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;/cdn-cgi/error/1015&amp;quot;\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;curl -s --compressed -H &amp;quot;Accept: application/json&amp;quot; -A &amp;quot;TestAgent/1.0&amp;quot; -H &amp;quot;Accept-Encoding: gzip, deflate&amp;quot; &amp;quot;&amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;/cdn-cgi/error/1015&amp;quot; | jq .\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;curl -s --compressed -H &amp;quot;Accept: application/problem+json&amp;quot; -A &amp;quot;TestAgent/1.0&amp;quot; -H &amp;quot;Accept-Encoding: gzip, deflate&amp;quot; &amp;quot;&amp;lt;YOUR_DOMAIN&amp;gt;/cdn-cgi/error/1015&amp;quot; | jq .\n&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;Error pages are the first conversation between Cloudflare and an agent. This launch makes that conversation structured, standards-compliant, and cheap to process.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To make this work across the web, agent runtimes should default to explicit structured &lt;code&gt;Accept&lt;/code&gt; headers, not bare &lt;code&gt;*/*&lt;/code&gt;. Use &lt;code&gt;Accept: text/markdown, */*&lt;/code&gt; for model-first workflows and &lt;code&gt;Accept: application/json, */*&lt;/code&gt; for typed control flow. If you maintain an agent framework, SDK, or browser automation stack, ship this default and treat bare &lt;code&gt;*/*&lt;/code&gt; as legacy fallback.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And it is only the first layer. We are building the rest of the agent stack on top of it: &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/ai-gateway/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;AI Gateway&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for routing, controls, and observability; &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/developer-platform/products/workers-ai/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Workers AI&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for inference; and the identity, security, and access primitives agents will need to operate safely at Internet scale.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflare is helping our customers deliver content in agent-friendly ways, and this is just the start. For the modern security team, the biggest challenge is no longer a lack of data; it is the overwhelming surplus of it. Most security professionals start their day navigating a sea of dashboards, hunting through disparate logs to answer a single, deceptively simple question: &amp;quot;What now?&amp;quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When you are forced to pivot between different tools just to identify a single misconfiguration, youâre losing the window of opportunity to prevent an incident. Thatâs why we built a revamped Security Overview dashboard: a single interface designed to empower defenders, by moving from reactive monitoring to proactive control.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/48MDFWpOUvJ1oHgj1SpHtf/6753298792d1a4cbfb7fb0766d255431/image7.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;BLOG-3168 image 1\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1921\&quot; height=\&quot;958\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;The new Security Overview dashboard.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;from-noise-to-action-rethinking-the-security-overview\&quot;&gt;From noise to action: rethinking the security overviewÂ &lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#from-noise-to-action-rethinking-the-security-overview\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Historically, dashboards focused on showing you &lt;i&gt;everything&lt;/i&gt; that was happening. But for a busy security analyst, the more important question is, &amp;quot;What do I need to fix right now?&amp;quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To solve this, we are introducing Security Action Items. This feature acts as a functional bridge between detection and investigation, surfacing vulnerabilities, so you no longer have to hunt for them. To help you triage effectively, items are ranked by criticality:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Critical: Urgent risks requiring immediate attention to prevent exploitation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Moderate: Issues that should be addressed to maintain a strong security posture.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Low: Best-practice optimizations and hardening suggestions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;By filtering by Insight Type (such as Suspicious Activity or Insecure Configuration), you can tailor your workflow to the specific threats your organization faces most.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/15hwrdwgNlDPvxCk96FZJr/7951b2e27767082b61d835e929d57bb9/image1.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1104\&quot; height=\&quot;555\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;One of the most common causes of a breach isn&amp;#39;t the absence of a security tool, itâs the fact that the tool was never turned on or was configured incorrectly. We call this the configuration gap.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The new Detection Tools module eliminates this blind spot. Instead of digging through nested settings pages to see if your traffic is actually being inspected, we provide a high-level status of your entire Cloudflare security stack in one view:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Are your primary shields active, or are you in &amp;quot;Log Only&amp;quot; mode during a period of increased volatility?Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Are you discovering shadow APIs, or are you flying blind?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;By surfacing these tools directly alongside your Security Action Items, we move the conversation from &lt;i&gt;&amp;quot;&lt;/i&gt;Do we have this tool?&amp;quot; to &amp;quot;Is this tool actively protecting us right now?&amp;quot;&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/yXmNWAN2vDNQ02fw2spLL/4ece4d88e8a58826e2c8f472ba9aaac9/Screenshot_2026-03-09_at_18.48.17.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;2014\&quot; height=\&quot;742\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;A high-level summary is only as good as the data behind it. To make the transition from a red flag to a solution seamless, we have unified the visibility of our Suspicious Activity cards. These cards now live in two strategic places: the Security Overview and the Security Analytics page.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you spot a Suspicious Activity card on your Overview page that piques your interest, there is no need to manually navigate to Analytics and re-create your filters. By clicking on the card, you are deep-linked directly into the Security Analytics dashboard with all the relevant filters automatically applied. This eliminates the &amp;quot;tab switching tax&amp;quot; that slows down incident response, keeping your workflow fluid and your response times fast.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;how-we-built-our-new-security-overview-dashboard\&quot;&gt;How we built our new security overview dashboard&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-we-built-our-new-security-overview-dashboard\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;To maintain a proactive defense, our engine produces and refreshes over 10 million actionable insights every day to ensure protection is always current.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Operating at this level presents two distinct engineering challenges. The first is scale: processing massive volumes of data seamlessly. The second and arguably harder challenge, is breadth. True security is horizontal, spanning your entire stack. To generate actionable insights that give you a comprehensive view of your risks and vulnerabilities, our engine must validate everything from simple SSL certificates to complex AI bot configurations.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To solve this, we built a system composed of smaller, specialized micro services, which we call checkers. Each checker is a subject-matter expert for a specific part of your stack, such as DNS records. The distribution of our checkers allows them to scale independently, hooked into the system in two ways: scheduled configuration checks or real-time listeners that flag a risk the instant an event occurs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;1. Scheduled checks&lt;/b&gt;: We deploy this mode for risks that need deep inspection. These are triggered by an orchestrator (scheduler), which periodically pushes tasks for the checkers to execute. We distribute the checker workload across a massively parallel system. For example, a task sent to the DNS checker might be: &amp;quot;Scan all the DNS related configurations of zone &lt;a href=\&quot;http://xyz.com\&quot;&gt;xyz.com&lt;/a&gt; and find anomalies.&amp;quot;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The checkers pick up these tasks independently. They use their specialized intelligence to scan through the assets and configurations. In the case of the DNS checker, it uses specialized and intelligent rules to scan all the DNS assets and configurations of a zone, be it A/AAAA/CNAME records or DMARC or SPF records.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is what the insight lifecycle looks like:Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The checker activates when a message is received.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The checker collects relevant assets (e.g., DNS records) about the zone or account.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The checker runs several checks to verify the status of the asset, e.g., if a CNAME record points to a server.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;If the state or configuration doesnât meet the required threshold, an insight is flagged.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;During the next check, if the insight persists, the timestamp is updated.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;If the insight has been remedied during the next check, it will be removed from the database.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1YwJ45kqLIdiHWoT29x6tR/13d3d31f58325776a781c7465d5f6aa3/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;2164\&quot; height=\&quot;1374\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;2. Event handlers: &lt;/b&gt;The checkers operate on a schedule round the clock, whereas the event handlers function in real-time. They listen to signals and events from our control plane.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6qUqsqqth0RZag7GDNeK1/8f09a8275d5ea8ca4223718e22c0e9f1/image5.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;830\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is what the real-time ruleset insight lifecycle looks like:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;A WAF rule configuration is modified.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;An event containing details of the change is triggered immediately.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The ruleset handler, which is actively listening, kicks into action.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The handler detects an anomaly, e.g, you have enabled the Cloudflare Managed Ruleset but left it in &amp;quot;Log Only&amp;quot; mode.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The handler deduces that the attacks are being recorded but not blocked.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The handler registers an insight and makes it available on the dashboard.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;If the configuration has been updated to a secure setting, the handler clears the insight.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt;The real-time nature of Ruleset handlers allow us to flag a misconfiguration or confirm a fix instantly.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;unifying-security-visibility-with-contextual-insights\&quot;&gt;Unifying security visibility with contextual insights&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#unifying-security-visibility-with-contextual-insights\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Our customers have consistently asked for more than just visibility: theyâve asked for context. While a notification that a record is misconfigured is helpful, itâs only half the story. To take immediate, confident action, defenders need to know the &amp;quot;so what?&amp;quot; including the business impact and the technical root cause. To address this, we have developed Contextual Insights for our detection engine. By surfacing data like traffic volume to a broken A record, we ensure that every insight is an invitation to act.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We are starting this journey of Contextual Insights by expanding the depth of our DNS insights. Instead of just flagging a broken record, we correlate the dangling signal with additional context and real-time traffic data to provide the âwhyâ and the âhowâ:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Target Context: We identify exactly which deleted resource (e.g., an old S3 bucket or cloud instance) the record points to.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Impact Context: We show you exactly how many users are still trying to reach that broken record.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letâs explore the âDangling A/AAAA/CNAME recordâ insights as an example.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To provide these insights, we must analyze the massive amount of data flowing through our network every second. To give you an idea of the work happening behind the scenes:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;100+ million DNS records are scanned weekly by our engine. In the past week, our engine identified over 1 million dangling DNS records. The majority (97%) are Dangling A/AAAA records and the remaining 3% are Dangling CNAME records.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Of the 31,000 dangling CNAME records:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;95% point to Microsoft Azure services.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;3% point to AWS Elastic Beanstalk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;This signals that these are high-priority targets for a subdomain takeover. An attacker can claim these abandoned cloud resources and immediately control your subdomain, allowing them to launch phishing attacks or spread misinformation under your trusted brand. With thousands of hits, a dangling record presents a high-priority risk for a subdomain takeover, necessitating immediate remediation to instantly gauge and mitigate the threat.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Our DNS checker uses a two-step process to generate these insights&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Step 1: Active Insight detection&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The checker starts verification as soon as it gets the message to start a scan. This process has been described in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://docs.google.com/document/d/1zpAjKdCU_80KZtIXwpHnlq05xGV54gTA-KehiOvlVc0/edit?tab=t.0#bookmark=id.fmv2o2tkjmvj\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;an earlier section&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Step 2: Contextual enrichment&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Once the insight is generated, the checkers gather relevant contextual data for the insight that helps the customer in understanding the impact of the security insight.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letâs explore in depth how the dangling DNS record insights are generated, focusing on the two-phase process involved.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6XNrfkKD9isLHsatUWb7tU/d8117d53a02e82b799da97563be30576/image3.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1097\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h4 id=\&quot;phase-1-active-verification\&quot;&gt;Phase 1: Active Verification&lt;/h4&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#phase-1-active-verification\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;A DNS record pointing to an IP address often looks perfectly valid on paper, even if the server behind it was decommissioned months ago. To confirm if a risk is real, our engine has to step outside the network and probe the destination in real-time. The checks performed can be categorized as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;The dead server check (A/AAAA records): &lt;/b&gt;For records pointing directly to IP addresses, we verify if the destination is still active. Our engine spins up a dedicated egress proxy to attempt a connection to the origin over HTTP and HTTPS. By using this special gateway, we simulate how a real user would connect from outside Cloudflareâs network. If the connection times out or the server returns a &amp;quot;404 Not Found&amp;quot; error, we confirm the resource is dead. This proves the DNS record is &amp;quot;dangling&amp;quot;, a live signpost pointing to an empty lot.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;The takeover check (CNAME records): &lt;/b&gt;Domain aliases (CNAMEs) often delegate traffic to third-party services, like a helpdesk or storage bucket. If you cancel that service but forget to delete the DNS record, you create a &amp;quot;dangling&amp;quot; link that attackers can claim.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To find these, our engine performs a 3-step process:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;First, we trace the chain by recursively resolving the CNAME record to find its final destination (e.g., &lt;code&gt;my-bucket.s3.amazonaws.com&lt;/code&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Next, we identify the provider by checking if that destination belongs to a known cloud service like AWS, Azure, or Shopify.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Finally, we confirm vacancy. Each cloud provider returns specific error patterns when a resource doesn&amp;#39;t existÂ  (e.g., S3&amp;#39;s &amp;quot;NoSuchBucket&amp;quot;). We probe the destination URL and match against these patterns to confirm if the resource is claimable.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt;If our engine detects that a resource has been released but the DNS record remains, we create an insight, prompting you to remove the record before an attacker can take over your subdomain.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h4 id=\&quot;phase-2-context-enrichment\&quot;&gt;Phase 2: Context Enrichment&lt;/h4&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#phase-2-context-enrichment\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Once a record is verified as broken, we add the necessary context to the insight that helps you take better action. The checker connects to different systems to gather the required context. For dangling insights, we focus on three critical dimensions:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Traffic Volume (The Impact) &lt;/b&gt;Our global ClickHouse clusters are a treasure trove of information. To understand if the record is actually in use, the checker queries our global ClickHouse clusters to sum up the total DNS queries for that record over the last 7 days. This valuable context lets you prioritize the remedy. A record with 0 queries can be fixed when you have time; a record with 10,000 queries is an active vulnerability that needs to be patched immediately.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Query to the clickhouse looks like:Â &lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT query_name,\n       sum(_sample_interval) as total\n  FROM &amp;lt;dnslogs_table_name&amp;gt;\n WHERE account_id = {{account_id}}\n   AND zone_id = {{zone_id}}\n   AND timestamp &amp;gt;= subtractDays(today(), 7)\n   AND timestamp &amp;lt; today()\n   AND query_name in (&amp;#039;{{record1}}&amp;#039;, &amp;#039;{{record2}}&amp;#039;, ...)\n GROUP BY query_name&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;The query asks âHow many times has this specific broken record been requested by real users in the last seven days?â&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Infrastructure owner (The Target) &lt;/b&gt;Knowing &lt;i&gt;who&lt;/i&gt; owns the destination infrastructure isÂ  Â  vital for both remediation and severity assessment.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;For IP records (A/AAAA):&lt;/b&gt; We identify the network owner (ASN) through the latest geolocation data from a Cloudflare &lt;b&gt;R2 bucket&lt;/b&gt; and performing high-speed lookups in memory. It tells you exactly where the dead resource lived (e.g., &amp;quot;Google Cloud&amp;quot; vs. &amp;quot;DigitalOcean&amp;quot;), speeding up your investigation.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;For CNAME Records:&lt;/b&gt; We identify the specific &lt;b&gt;Hosting Provider&lt;/b&gt; (e.g., AWS S3, Shopify). This dictates the risk level. If a record points to a provider known for easy takeovers (like S3), we mark it as &lt;b&gt;Critical&lt;/b&gt;; otherwise, it is &lt;b&gt;Moderate&lt;/b&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;DNS TTL &lt;/b&gt;We also extract the TTL (Time To Live) value directly from the record configuration.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;This tells you the &amp;quot;lag time&amp;quot; of your fix. If you delete a dangling record with a high TTL (e.g., 24 hours), it will remain cached in resolvers around the world for a full day, meaning the vulnerability stays open even after you patch it. Knowing this helps you manage expectations during an incident response.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;looking-forward\&quot;&gt;Looking forward&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#looking-forward\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;While this experience is launching at the domain level today, we know that for enterprise customers, security isn&amp;#39;t managed just one domain at a time. Our roadmap is focused on bringing this intelligence to the account level next. Soon, security teams can use a centralized view that aggregates security action items and prioritizes the most critical risks to remediate across all of their Cloudflare domains.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Security shouldn&amp;#39;t feel like a game of catch-up. performance.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;HTTP Requests&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;As the most comprehensive dataset, it serves as the &amp;quot;primary record&amp;quot; of all application-layer traffic, enabling the reconstruction of session activity, exploit attempts, and bot patterns.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Firewall Events&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides critical evidence of blocked or challenged threats, allowing analysts to identify the specific WAF rules, IP reputations, or custom filters that intercepted an attack.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;DNS Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Identify cache poisoning attempts, domain hijacking, and infrastructure-level reconnaissance by tracking every query resolved at the authoritative edge.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;NEL (Network Error Logging) Reports&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Distinguish between a coordinated Layer 7 DDoS attack and legitimate network connectivity issues by tracking client-side browser errors.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Spectrum Events&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;For non-web applications, these logs provide visibility into L4 traffic (TCP/UDP), helping to identify anomalies or brute-force attacks against protocols like SSH, RDP, or custom gaming traffic.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Page Shield&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Track and audit unauthorized changes to your site&amp;#39;s client-side environment such as JavaScript, outbound connections.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Zaraz Events&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Examine how third-party tools and trackers are interacting with user data, which is vital for auditing privacy compliance and detecting unauthorized script behaviors.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h4 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Focus: Internal security, Zero Trust, administrative changes, and network activity.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Access Requests&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks identity-based authentication events to determine which users accessed specific internal applications and whether those attempts were authorized.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Audit Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides a trail of configuration changes within the Cloudflare dashboard to identify unauthorized administrative actions or modifications.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;CASB Findings&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Identifies security misconfigurations and data risks within SaaS applications (like Google Drive or Microsoft 365) to prevent unauthorized data exposure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Magic Transit / IPSec Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Helps network engineers perform network-level (L3) monitoring such as reviewing tunnel health and view BGP routing changes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Browser Isolation Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks user actions &lt;i&gt;inside&lt;/i&gt; an isolated browser session (e.g., copy-paste, print, or file uploads) to prevent data leaks on untrusted sitesÂ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Device Posture ResultsÂ &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Details the security health and compliance status of devices connecting to your network, helping to identify compromised or non-compliant endpoints.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;DEX Application TestsÂ &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Monitors application performance from the user&amp;#39;s perspective, which can help distinguish between a security-related outage and a standard performance degradation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;DEX Device State Events&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides telemetry on the physical state of user devices, useful for correlating hardware or OS-level anomalies with potential security incidents.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;DNS Firewall Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks DNS queries filtered through the DNS Firewall to identify communication with known malicious domains or command-and-control (C2) servers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Email Security Alerts&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Logs malicious email activity and phishing attempts detected at the gateway to trace the origin of email-based entry vectors.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Gateway DNS&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Monitors every DNS query made by users on your network to identify shadow IT, malware callbacks, or domain-generation algorithms (DGAs).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Gateway HTTP&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides full visibility into encrypted and unencrypted web traffic to detect hidden payloads, malicious file downloads, or unauthorized SaaS usage.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Gateway Network&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks L3/L4 network traffic (non-HTTP) to identify unauthorized port usage, protocol anomalies, or lateral movement within the network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;IPSec Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Monitors the status and traffic of encrypted site-to-site tunnels to ensure the integrity and availability of secure network connections.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Magic IDS Detections&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Surfaces matches against intrusion detection signatures to alert investigators to known exploit patterns or malware behavior traversing the network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Network Analytics Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Provides high-level visibility into packet-level data to identify volumetric DDoS attacks or unusual traffic spikes targeting specific infrastructure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Sinkhole HTTP Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Captures traffic directed to &amp;quot;sinkholed&amp;quot; IP addresses to confirm which internal devices are attempting to communicate with known botnet infrastructure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;WARP Config Changes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tracks modifications to the WARP client settings on end-user devices to ensure that security agents haven&amp;#39;t been tampered with or disabled.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;WARP Toggle Changes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Specifically logs when users enable or disable their secure connectivity, helping to identify periods where a device may have been unprotected.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Zero Trust Network Session Logs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Logs the duration and status of authenticated user sessions to map out the complete lifecycle of a user&amp;#39;s access within the protected perimeter.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;log-explorer-can-identify-malicious-activity-at-every-stage\&quot;&gt;Log Explorer can identify malicious activity at every stage&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#log-explorer-can-identify-malicious-activity-at-every-stage\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Get granular application layer visibility with &lt;b&gt;HTTP Requests&lt;/b&gt;, &lt;b&gt;Firewall Events&lt;/b&gt;, and &lt;b&gt;DNS logs&lt;/b&gt; to see exactly how traffic is hitting your public-facing properties.&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;Track internal movement with &lt;b&gt;Access
