If a credential is compromised, youâll see where they went. Use &lt;b&gt;Magic IDS&lt;/b&gt; and &lt;b&gt;Network Analytics logs&lt;/b&gt; to spot volumetric attacks and &amp;quot;East-West&amp;quot; lateral movement within your private network.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;identify-the-reconnaissance\&quot;&gt;Identify the reconnaissance&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#identify-the-reconnaissance\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Attackers use scanners and other tools to look for entry points, hidden directories, or software vulnerabilities. To identify this, using Log Explorer, you can query &lt;code&gt;http_requests&lt;/code&gt; for any &lt;code&gt;EdgeResponseStatus&lt;/code&gt; codes of 401, 403, or 404 coming from a single IP, or requests to sensitive paths (e.g. &lt;code&gt;/.env&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;/.git&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;/wp-admin&lt;/code&gt;).Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Additionally, &lt;code&gt;magic_ids_detections&lt;/code&gt; logs can also be used to identify scanning at the network layer. These logs provide packet-level visibility into threats targeting your network. Unlike standard HTTP logs, these logs focus on &lt;b&gt;signature-based detections&lt;/b&gt; at the network and transport layers (IP, TCP, UDP). Query to discover cases where a single &lt;code&gt;SourceIP&lt;/code&gt; is triggering multiple unique detections across a wide range of &lt;code&gt;DestinationPort&lt;/code&gt; values in a short timeframe. Magic IDS signatures can specifically flag activities like Nmap scans or SYN stealth scans.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;check-for-diversions\&quot;&gt;Check for diversions&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#check-for-diversions\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;While the attacker is conducting reconnaissance, they may attempt to disguise this with a simultaneous network flood. Pivot to &lt;code&gt;network_analytics_logs&lt;/code&gt; to see if a volumetric attack is being used as a smokescreen.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;identify-the-approach\&quot;&gt;Identify the approachÂ &lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#identify-the-approach\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Once attackers identify a potential vulnerability, they begin to craft their weapon. The attacker sends malicious payloads (e.g. SQL injection or large/corrupt file uploads) to confirm the vulnerability. Review &lt;code&gt;http_requests&lt;/code&gt; and/or &lt;code&gt;fw_events&lt;/code&gt; to identify any Cloudflare detection tools that have triggered. Cloudflare logs security signals in these datasets to easily identify requests with malicious payloads using fields such as &lt;code&gt;WAFAttackScore&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;WAFSQLiAttackScore&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;FraudAttack&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;ContentScanJobResults&lt;/code&gt;, and several more. Review &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/logpush/logpush-job/datasets/zone/http_requests/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;our documentation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to get a full understanding of these fields. The &lt;code&gt;fw_events&lt;/code&gt; logs can be used to determine whether these requests made it past Cloudflareâs defenses by examining the &lt;code&gt;action&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;source&lt;/code&gt;, and &lt;code&gt;ruleID&lt;/code&gt; fields. Cloudflareâs managed rules by default blocks many of these payloads by default. Review Application Security Overview to know if your application is protected.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1zpFguYrnbOPwyASGQCqZK/63f398acce2226e453a5eea1cc749241/image3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;Showing the Managed rules Insight that displays on Security Overview if the current zone does not have Managed Rules enabled\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1117\&quot; height=\&quot;124\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Showing the Managed rules Insight that displays on Security Overview if the current zone does not have Managed Rules enabled&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;audit-the-identity\&quot;&gt;Audit the identity&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#audit-the-identity\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Did that suspicious IP manage to log in? Use the &lt;code&gt;ClientIP&lt;/code&gt; to search &lt;code&gt;access_requests&lt;/code&gt;. If you see a &amp;quot;&lt;code&gt;Decision: Allow&lt;/code&gt;&amp;quot; for a sensitive internal app, you know you have a compromised account.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;stop-the-leak-data-exfiltration\&quot;&gt;Stop the leak (data exfiltration)&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#stop-the-leak-data-exfiltration\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Attackers sometimes use DNS tunneling to bypass firewalls by encoding sensitive data (like passwords or SSH keys) into DNS queries. Instead of a normal request like &lt;code&gt;google.com&lt;/code&gt;, the logs will show long, encoded strings. Look for an unusually high volume of queries for unique, long, and high-entropy subdomains by examining the fields: &lt;code&gt;QueryName&lt;/code&gt;: Look for strings like &lt;a href=\&quot;http://h3ldo293js92.example.com\&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;&lt;u&gt;h3ldo293js92.example.com&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;code&gt;QueryType&lt;/code&gt;: Often uses &lt;code&gt;TXT&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;CNAME&lt;/code&gt;, or &lt;code&gt;NULL&lt;/code&gt; records to carry the payload, and &lt;code&gt;ClientIP&lt;/code&gt;: Identify if a single internal host is generating thousands of these unique requests.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Additionally, attackers may attempt to leak sensitive data by hiding it within non-standard protocols or by using common protocols (like DNS or ICMP) in unusual ways to bypass standard firewalls. Discover this by querying the &lt;code&gt;magic_ids_detections&lt;/code&gt; logs to look for signatures that flag protocol anomalies, such as &amp;quot;ICMP tunneling&amp;quot; or &amp;quot;DNS tunneling&amp;quot; detections in the &lt;code&gt;SignatureMessage&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Whether you are investigating a zero-day vulnerability or tracking a sophisticated botnet, the data you need is now at your fingertips.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;correlate-across-datasets\&quot;&gt;Correlate across datasets&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#correlate-across-datasets\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Investigate malicious activity across multiple datasets by pivoting between multiple concurrent searches. With Log Explorer, you can now work with multiple queries simultaneously with the new Tabs feature. Switch between tabs to query different datasets or Pivot and adjust queries using filtering via your query results.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div style=\&quot;position: relative; padding-top: 45.348837209302324%;\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;iframe\n    src=\&quot;https://customer-eq7kiuol0tk9chox.cloudflarestream.com/fdce57563737015fcb27147c4b44ac70/iframe?muted=true&amp;preload=true&amp;loop=true&amp;autoplay=true&amp;poster=https%3A%2F%2Fcustomer-eq7kiuol0tk9chox.cloudflarestream.com%2Ffdce57563737015fcb27147c4b44ac70%2Fthumbnails%2Fthumbnail.jpg%3Ftime%3D%26height%3D600\&quot;\n    loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;\n    style=\&quot;border: none; position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; height: 100%; width: 100%;\&quot;\n    allow=\&quot;accelerometer; gyroscope; autoplay; encrypted-media; picture-in-picture;\&quot;\n    allowfullscreen=\&quot;true\&quot;\n  &gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When you correlate data across multiple Cloudflare log sources, you can detect sophisticated multi-stage attacks that appear benign when viewed in isolation. This cross-dataset analysis allows you to see the full attack chain from reconnaissance to exfiltration.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;session-hijacking-token-theft\&quot;&gt;Session hijacking (token theft)&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#session-hijacking-token-theft\&quot; A user authenticates via Cloudflare Access, but their subsequent HTTP_request traffic looks like a bot.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 1:&lt;/b&gt; Identify high-risk sessions in &lt;code&gt;http_requests&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT RayID, ClientIP, ClientRequestUserAgent, BotScore\nFROM http_requests\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND BotScore &amp;lt; 20 \nLIMIT 100&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 2:&lt;/b&gt; Copy the &lt;code&gt;RayID&lt;/code&gt; and search &lt;code&gt;access_requests&lt;/code&gt; \n  AND RayID = &amp;#039;INSERT_RAY_ID_HERE&amp;#039;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;post-phishing-c2-beaconing\&quot;&gt;Post-phishing C2 beaconing&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#post-phishing-c2-beaconing\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; An employee clicked a link in a phishing email which resulted in compromising their workstation. This workstation sends a DNS query for a known malicious domain, then immediately triggers an IDS alert.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 1:&lt;/b&gt; Find phishing attacks by examining email_security_alerts for violations.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT Timestamp, Threatcategories, To, Alertreason\nFROM email_security_alerts\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND Threatcategories LIKE &amp;#039;phishing&amp;#039;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 2:&lt;/b&gt; Use Access logs to correlate the userâs email (To) to their IP Address.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT Email, IPAddress\nFROM access_requests\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 3:&lt;/b&gt; Find internal IPs querying a specific malicious domain in &lt;code&gt;gateway_dns&lt;/code&gt; logs.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;\nSELECT SrcIP, QueryName, DstIP, \nFROM gateway_dns\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND SrcIP = &amp;#039;INSERT_IP_FROM_PREVIOUS_QUERY&amp;#039;\n  AND QueryName LIKE &amp;#039;%malicious_domain_name%&amp;#039;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;lateral-movement-access-network-probing\&quot;&gt;Lateral movement (Access â network probing)&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#lateral-movement-access-network-probing\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Scenario:&lt;/b&gt; A user logs in via Zero Trust and then tries to scan the internal network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 1:&lt;/b&gt; Find successful logins from unexpected locations in &lt;code&gt;access_requests&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT IPAddress, Email, Country\nFROM access_requests\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND Allowed = true \n  AND Country != &amp;#039;US&amp;#039; -- Replace with your HQ country&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Step 2:&lt;/b&gt; Check if that &lt;code&gt;IPAddress&lt;/code&gt; is triggering network-level signatures in &lt;code&gt;magic_ids_detections&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-SQL\&quot;&gt;SELECT SignatureMessage, DestinationIP, Protocol\nFROM magic_ids_detections\nWHERE date = &amp;#039;2026-02-22&amp;#039; \n  AND SourceIP = &amp;#039;INSERT_IP_ADDRESS_HERE&amp;#039;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;opening-doors-for-more-data\&quot;&gt;Opening doors for more dataÂ &lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#opening-doors-for-more-data\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;From the beginning, Log Explorer was designed with extensibility in mind. Every dataset schema is defined using JSON Schema, a widely-adopted standard for describing the structure and types of JSON data. This design decision has enabled us to easily expand beyond HTTP Requests and Firewall Events to the full breadth of Cloudflare&amp;#39;s telemetry. The same schema-driven approach that powered our initial datasets scaled naturally to accommodate Zero Trust logs, network analytics, email security alerts, and everything in between.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;More importantly, this standardization opens the door to ingesting data beyond Cloudflare&amp;#39;s native telemetry. Because our ingestion pipeline is schema-driven rather than hard-coded, we&amp;#39;re positioned to accept any structured data that can be expressed in JSON format. For security teams managing hybrid environments, this means Log Explorer could eventually serve as a single pane of glass, correlating Cloudflare&amp;#39;s edge telemetry with logs from third-party sources, all queryable through the same SQL interface. While today&amp;#39;s release focuses on completing coverage of Cloudflare&amp;#39;s product portfolio, the architectural groundwork is laid for a future where customers can bring their own data sources with custom schemas.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;faster-data-faster-response-architectural-upgrades\&quot;&gt;Faster data, faster response: architectural upgrades&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#faster-data-faster-response-architectural-upgrades\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;To investigate a multi-vector attack effectively, timing is everything. A delay of even a few minutes in the log availability can be the difference between proactive defense and reactive damage control.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That is why we have optimized our ingestion for better speed and resilience. By increasing concurrency in one part of our ingestion path, we have eliminated bottlenecks that could cause ânoisy neighborâ issues, ensuring that one clientâs data surge doesnât slow down anotherâs visibility. This architectural work has reduced our P99 ingestion latency by approximately 55%, and our P50 by 25%, cutting the time it takes for an event at the edge to become available for your SQL queries.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/41M2eWP0BwrQFSZW4GzZbV/7a6139354abb561aba17e77d83beb17a/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;Grafana chart displaying the drop in ingest latency after architectural upgrades\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;882\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Grafana chart displaying the drop in ingest latency after architectural upgrades&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;follow-along-for-more-updates\&quot;&gt;Follow along for more updates&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#follow-along-for-more-updates\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;We&amp;#39;re just getting started. href="https://www.cloudflare.com/demos/protect-ai-apps/"><u>AI Security for Apps</u></a> detects and mitigates threats to AI-powered applications. Today, we&#39;re announcing that it is generally available.</p><p>Weâre shipping with new capabilities like detection for custom topics, and we&#39;re making AI endpoint discovery free for every Cloudflare customerâincluding those on Free, Pro, and Business plansâto give everyone visibility into where AI is deployed across their Internet-facing apps.</p><p>We&#39;re also announcing an expanded collaboration with IBM, which has chosen Cloudflare to deliver AI security to its cloud customers. And weâre partnering with Wiz to give mutual customers a unified view of their AI security posture.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h2 id="a-new-kind-of-attack-surface">A new kind of attack surface</h2>
      <a href="#a-new-kind-of-attack-surface" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>Traditional web applications have defined operations: check a bank balance, make a transfer. You can write deterministic rules to secure those interactions.Â </p><p>AI-powered applications and agents are different. They accept natural language and generate unpredictable responses. There&#39;s no fixed set of operations to allow or deny, because the inputs and outputs are probabilistic. Attackers can manipulate large language models to take unauthorized actions or leak sensitive data. Prompt injection, sensitive information disclosure, and unbounded consumption are just a few of the risks cataloged in the <a href="https://genai.owasp.org/llm-top-10/"><u>OWASP Top 10 for LLM Applications</u></a>.</p><p>These risks escalate as AI applications become agents. When an AI gains access to tool callsâprocessing refunds, modifying accounts, providing discounts, or accessing customer dataâa single malicious prompt becomes an immediate security incident.</p><p>Customers tell us what theyâre up against. &quot;Most of Newfold Digital&#39;s teams are putting in their own Generative AI safeguards, but everybody is innovating so quickly that there are inevitably going to be some gaps eventually,â says Rick Radinger, Principal Systems Architect at Newfold Digital, which operates Bluehost, HostGator, and Domain.com. </p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h2 id="what-ai-security-for-apps-does">What AI Security for Apps does</h2>
      <a href="#what-ai-security-for-apps-does" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>We built AI Security for Apps to address this. It sits in front of your AI-powered applications, whether you&#39;re using a third-party model or hosting your own, as part of Cloudflare&#39;s <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/cdn/glossary/reverse-proxy/"><u>reverse proxy</u></a>. It helps you (1) discover AI-powered apps across your web property, (2) detect malicious or off-policy behavior to those endpoints, and (3) mitigate threats via the familiar WAF rule builder. </p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5xpmckBUupzELjYOSx5bAF/cace1ab2ed2dd54d8d7a7ff60587ef65/BLOG-3128_2.png" alt="BLOG-3128 2" class="kg-image" width="1999" height="650" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h3 id="discovery-now-free-for-everyone">Discovery â now free for everyone</h3>
      <a href="#discovery-now-free-for-everyone" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>Before you can protect your LLM-powered applications, you need to know where they&#39;re being used. We often hear from security teams who donât have a complete picture of AI deployments across their apps, especially as the LLM market evolves and developers swap out models and providers.Â </p><p>AI Security for Apps automatically identifies LLM-powered endpoints across your web properties, regardless of where theyâre hosted or what the model is. Starting today, this capability is free for every Cloudflare customer, including Free, Pro, and Business plans.Â </p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2dBKhU5VNbzAePDAnaHkTK/3f6a569e495e03c3e2afca4d6183e02d/image4.png" alt="BLOG-3128 3" class="kg-image" width="1999" height="1000" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p><sup><i>Cloudflareâs dashboard page of web assets, showing 2 example endpoints labelled as </i></sup><code><sup><i>cf-llm</i></sup></code></p><p>Discovering these endpoints automatically requires more than matching common path patterns like <code>/chat/completions</code>. Many AI-powered applications don&#39;t have a chat interface: think product search, property valuation tools, or recommendation engines. We built a <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/take-control-of-public-ai-application-security-with-cloudflare-firewall-for-ai/#discovering-llm-powered-applications"><u>detection system that looks at how endpoints behave</u></a>, not what they&#39;re called. To confidently identify AI-powered endpoints, <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/api-shield/security/api-discovery/#requirements"><u>sufficient valid traffic</u></a> is required.</p><p>AI-powered endpoints that have been discovered will be visible under <a href="https://dash.cloudflare.com/?to=/:account/:zone/security/web-assets"><u>Security â Web Assets</u></a>, labeled as <code>cf-llm</code>. For customers on a Free plan, endpoint discovery is initiated when you first navigate to the <a href="https://dash.cloudflare.com/?to=/:account/:zone/security/web-assets/discovery"><u>Discovery page</u></a>. For customers on a paid plan, discovery occurs automatically in the background on a recurring basis. If your AI-powered endpoints have been discovered, you can review them immediately.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h3 id="detection">Detection</h3>
      <a href="#detection" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>AI Security for Apps detections follow the <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/detections/"><u>always-on approach</u></a> for traffic to your AI-powered endpoints. Each prompt is run through multiple detection modules for prompt injection, PII exposure, and sensitive or toxic topics. The resultsâwhether the prompt was malicious or notâare attached as metadata you can use in custom WAF rules to enforce your policies. We are continuously exploring ways to leverage our global network, which sees traffic from roughly <a href="https://w3techs.com/technologies/history_overview/proxy/all"><u>20% of the web</u></a>, to identify new attack patterns across millions of sites before they reach yours.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7oGjcaUL5L9zlAkz8lSmXv/4354a9555135e19de5c93d3d113e6790/BLOG-3128_4.png" alt="BLOG-3128 4" class="kg-image" width="1922" height="444" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h4 id="new-in-ga-custom-topics-detection">New in GA: Custom topics detection</h4>
      <a href="#new-in-ga-custom-topics-detection" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>The product ships with built-in detection for common threats: prompt injections, <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/take-control-of-public-ai-application-security-with-cloudflare-firewall-for-ai/#detecting-prompts-designed-to-leak-pii"><u>PII extraction</u></a>, and <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/block-unsafe-llm-prompts-with-firewall-for-ai/"><u>toxic topics</u></a>. But every business has its own definition of what&#39;s off-limits. A financial services company might need to detect discussions of specific securities. A healthcare company might need to flag conversations that touch on patient data. A retailer might want to know when customers are asking about competitor products.</p><p>The new custom topics feature lets you define these categories. You specify the topic, we inspect the prompt and output a relevance score that you can use to log, block, or handle however you decide. Our goal is to build an extensible tool that flexes to your use cases.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1WzPhy11ZmUXDGZjft4sY1/7ebfafaf2114eaba83a829694837fc2c/image1.png" alt="BLOG-3128 5" class="kg-image" width="1946" height="819" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p><sup><i>Prompt relevance score inside of AI Security for Apps</i></sup></p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h4 id="new-in-ga-custom-prompt-extraction">New in GA: Custom prompt extraction</h4>
      <a href="#new-in-ga-custom-prompt-extraction" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>AI Security for Apps enforces guardrails before unsafe prompts can reach your infrastructure. To run detections accurately and provide real-time protection, we first need to identify the prompt within the request payload. Prompts can live anywhere in a request body, and different LLM providers structure their APIs differently. OpenAI and most providers use <code>$.messages[*].content</code> for chat completions. Anthropic&#39;s batch API nests prompts inside <code>$.requests[*].params.messages[*].content</code>. Your custom property valuation tool might use <code>$.property_description</code>.</p><p>Out of the box, we support the standard formats used by OpenAI, Anthropic, Google Gemini, Mistral, Cohere, xAI, DeepSeek, and others. When we can&#39;t match a known pattern, we apply a default-secure posture and run detection on the entire request body. This can introduce false positives when the payload contains fields that are sensitive but don&#39;t feed directly to an AI model, for example, a <code>$.customer_name</code> field alongside the actual prompt might trigger PII detection unnecessarily.</p><p>Soon, you&#39;ll be able to define your own JSONPath expressions to tell us exactly where to find the prompt. This will reduce false positives and lead to more accurate detections. We&#39;re also building a prompt-learning capability that will automatically adapt to your application&#39;s structure over time.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h3 id="mitigation">Mitigation</h3>
      <a href="#mitigation" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>Once a threat is identified and scored, you can block it, log it, or deliver custom responses, using the same WAF rules engine you already use for the rest of your application security. The power of Cloudflareâs shared platform is that you can combine AI-specific signals with everything else we know about a request, represented by <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/ruleset-engine/rules-language/fields/reference/"><u>hundreds of fields</u></a> available in the WAF. A prompt injection attempt is suspicious. A prompt injection attempt from an IP thatâs been probing your login page, using a browser fingerprint associated with previous attacks, and rotating through a botnet is a different story. Point solutions that only see the AI layer canât make these connections.</p><p>This unified security layer is exactly what they need at Newfold Digital to discover, label, and protect AI endpoints, says Radinger: âWe look forward to using it across all these projects to serve as a fail-safe.&quot;</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h2 id="growing-ecosystem">Growing ecosystem</h2>
      <a href="#growing-ecosystem" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>AI Security for Applications will also be available through Cloudflare&#39;s growing ecosystem, including through integration with IBM Cloud. Through <a href="https://www.ibm.com/products/cloud-internet-services"><u>IBM Cloud Internet Services (CIS)</u></a>, end users can already procure advanced application security solutions and manage them directly through their IBM Cloud account.Â </p><p>We&#39;re also partnering with Wiz to connect AI Security for Applications with <a href="https://www.wiz.io/solutions/ai-spm"><u>Wiz AI Security</u></a>, giving mutual customers a unified view of their AI security posture, from model and agent discovery in the cloud to application-layer guardrails at the edge.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h2 id="how-to-get-started">How to get started</h2>
      <a href="#how-to-get-started" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>AI Security for Apps is available now for Cloudflareâs Enterprise customers. Contact your account team to get started, or see the product in action with a <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/demos/protect-ai-apps/"><u>self-guided tour</u></a>.</p><p>If you&#39;re on a Free, Pro, or Business plan, you can use AI endpoint discovery today. Log in to your dashboard and navigate to <b>Security â Web Assets</b> to see which endpoints we&#39;ve identified. Keep an eye out â we plan to make all AI Security for Apps capabilities available for customers on all plans soon.</p><p>For configuration details, see our <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/waf/detections/firewall-for-ai/"><u>documentation</u></a>.</p></div></section><section class="post-full-content flex flex-row flex-wrap mw7 center mb4"><div class="post-content lh-copy w-100 gray1 bt b--gray8 pt4">Cloudflare's connectivity cloud protects <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/network-services/' rel='noreferrer'>entire corporate networks</a>, helps customers build <a target='_blank' href='https://workers.cloudflare.com/' rel='noreferrer'>Internet-scale applications efficiently</a>, accelerates any <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/performance/accelerate-internet-applications/' rel='noreferrer'>website or Internet application</a>, <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/ddos/' rel='noreferrer'>wards off DDoS attacks</a>, keeps <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/application-security/' rel='noreferrer'>hackers at bay</a>, and can help you on <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/products/zero-trust/' rel='noreferrer'>your journey to Zero Trust</a>.<br/><br/>Visit <a target='_blank' href='https://one.one.one.one/' rel='noreferrer'>1.1.1.1</a> from any device to get started with our free app that makes your Internet faster and safer.<br/><br/>To learn more about our mission to help build a better Internet, <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/what-is-cloudflare/' rel='noreferrer'>start here</a>.
